<div id="review_109676084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109676084" />
    <a title="cara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3081426-cara"><img alt="cara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496890211p2/3081426.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109676084?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="cara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="cara" href="/user/show/3081426-cara">cara</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081426-cara?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3081426-cara?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109676084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7011116578224005770">Thirteen Days to Midnight is, in one word, incredible. <br/><br/>The story opens with our protag., Jacob, returning to his private school, Holy Cross, after a week long break due to a traumatic event. A few pages after this scene I realized that my eyes were glued to the novel and weren't, not even for sleep, going anywhere. Carman's characters draw you in and the intensity of the plot keeps you there.<br/><br/>The adventure Jacob, Milo, & Oh find themselves 'dragged' into is dangerous in the way that motorcycles a</span>
  <span id="freeText7011116578224005770" style="display:none">Thirteen Days to Midnight is, in one word, incredible. <br /><br />The story opens with our protag., Jacob, returning to his private school, Holy Cross, after a week long break due to a traumatic event. A few pages after this scene I realized that my eyes were glued to the novel and weren't, not even for sleep, going anywhere. Carman's characters draw you in and the intensity of the plot keeps you there.<br /><br />The adventure Jacob, Milo, &amp; Oh find themselves 'dragged' into is dangerous in the way that motorcycles are dangerous. If used correctly, with the right gear &amp; proper training, they're not dangerous at all. But, when put into the hands of let's say three teenagers, things can get very dangerous. Something stirs inside the teens, something that makes them want to push the bike's limits, test how hard they can push it, how fast it can go. A feeling gives them the urge to want to do things that may be fun for a while, but they know shouldn't be messed with. Temptation.<br /><br />Temptation is found in many places &amp; can take many forms. The most dangerous kind of temptation is the temptation of teenagers with power. Face it, we're moody, hate to be told what to do, &amp; act irrationally and emotionally nine times out of ten. (Hormones, people, they're always pumping.) When Jacob and his friends are given power, they react irrationally and get themselves into a pickle. A big one...we're talking Guiness Book of World Records sized pickle. Yeah, they screw up a bit.<br /><br />The way the three friends handle everything feels very natural, logical. They act like you'd expect them to react, emotionally, irrationally. This works because they are teenagers, and they will make mistakes. Instead of sitting around on their arses and weeping though, they take action and get things done. <br /><br />The characters in Thirteen Days are strong willed, smart, fierce, and funny. They make you care what happens in the storyline, what happens to them. Jacob, Milo, Oh, &amp; even Father Tim breathe, and give this book exactly what it needs to earn a 5 star rating from me.<br /><br /><br />Summing it up:<br /><br />Please, do yourself a favor. Get this book now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7011116578224005770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2020943867" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2020943867" />
    <a title="Tessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47669419-tessa"><img alt="Tessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549384978p2/47669419.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2020943867?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tessa" href="/user/show/47669419-tessa">Tessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2020943867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer671650463415148589">2.5 stars<br/><br/>The second half of the book really picked up the pace and it got quite interesting- but there were just too many things that didn't sit right with me.<br/><br/>The whole debate about animals not having emotions for example is just something that really pissed me off. I don't think it was necessary to include in this book and it's just not an opinion people should have. (I mean what the hell? How arrogant can humans be?)<br/>Then there were all these instances where Jakob talked about how pretty, beaut</span>
  <span id="freeText671650463415148589" style="display:none">2.5 stars<br /><br />The second half of the book really picked up the pace and it got quite interesting- but there were just too many things that didn't sit right with me.<br /><br />The whole debate about animals not having emotions for example is just something that really pissed me off. I don't think it was necessary to include in this book and it's just not an opinion people should have. (I mean what the hell? How arrogant can humans be?)<br />Then there were all these instances where Jakob talked about how pretty, beautiful, hot, perfect, etc. etc. Ophelia was instead of focusing on her personality. She could literally be going mad with the need to kill herself and he was only whining about how she was still beautiful, despite her dead eyes. Seriously?<br /><br />I also thought the whole "You're indestructable." is kind of too easy to tranfer a superpower- and I thought the rules behind it were kind of weird. Also if some guy managed to force this power into his soul, don't you think you could do some research and find a way to get rid of it again?<br /><br />The thing that bothered me the most, though, is this mindset that a lot of people seem to have: There is nothing worse than death. Which is ignorant, stupid and wrong. Ophelia was literally being tortured by the darkness and death inside of her, <i>so much that she wanted to <b>die</b> </i> and the two male main characters were like "well, at least she won't be able to kill herself if we keep her indestructable". I'm sorry to tell you this, but that's not heroic, mercyful or selfless. If they are suffering so badly that they are as desperate as poor Ophelia was, you need to let them die, you need to stop forcing them into something they don't want. How can you say you love someone if you want them to live only so you won't feel bad?<br /><br />I do think that the whole superpower plot was well-wrought and interesting. The characters weren't the best and most of them fit these "stuck-up brutal stupid jock" or "brainless hot bitch" or "stupidly brave goodnatured hot MC who's also somehow a helpless baby and needs the male MC to protect her" stereotypes. The writing wasn't spectacular but also definitely not bad.</span>
  <a data-text-id="671650463415148589" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98962338" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98962338" />
    <a title="Katie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343589-katie"><img alt="Katie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486578421p2/1343589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98962338?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie" href="/user/show/1343589-katie">Katie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer98962338&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98962338" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6517689010184000150">This review has spoilers of the ending of the book. Don't read on if that bothers you.<br/><br/>This book was intriguing and I liked the premise, but I had quite a few problems with it.<br/><br/>First, I disliked the love interest, Ophelia, intensely. I had no idea why the main character, who was otherwise pretty smart, fell so hard for this annoying, selfish, bullying girl in like, one day. <br/><br/>My second complaint is that the book is written in first person but the main character keeps secrets throughout the book. He </span>
  <span id="freeText6517689010184000150" style="display:none">This review has spoilers of the ending of the book. Don't read on if that bothers you.<br /><br />This book was intriguing and I liked the premise, but I had quite a few problems with it.<br /><br />First, I disliked the love interest, Ophelia, intensely. I had no idea why the main character, who was otherwise pretty smart, fell so hard for this annoying, selfish, bullying girl in like, one day. <br /><br />My second complaint is that the book is written in first person but the main character keeps secrets throughout the book. He is not an unreliable narrator (like Liar by Justine Larbalestier), he just conveniently doesn't think of things until he tells them to his friend later. Or he'll think, "but I knew a secret..." which is a total cop out. If you're writing in first person the reader should know what the character knows.<br /><br />Also, the ending wrapped up too fast and made no sense. Jacob finds a letter from his foster dad explaining all this stuff that had little foreshadowing (hello exposition dump). The idea that you had to kill the person you loaned the power to the number of times they had tried to die made no sense. What happens if you don't do it and they come back to life? It is never clear what the consequences are. (I kinda hoped Ophelia would come back as a zombie to see what the danger was.) <br /><br />And why didn't Jacob's foster dad come back to life? Did they have to kill Oh for just her own deaths or for all of the times Jacob loaned the power to anyone? Why would those deaths be on her and not the other person, or on Jacob himself? Am I missing something here or was it just not explained well at all?<br /><br />Overall it was an OK book but it could have used better foreshadowing and buildup to the climax. Also, the title (and the chapter titles) had nothing to do with the book. They should have called it Invincible, or Loaner, or Invulnerable, or something. I kept hoping there was some secret meaning to Midnight but no, it was just when the climax happened. Bah!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6517689010184000150" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19765124-thirteen-days-to-midnight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7982709-sh-e-reader?shelf=library-eborrow">library-eborrow</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7697712132316795813">Huh ... I'm really not sure I understood what happened there in the last half of the book, but as I was pushing to even finish, I'm certainly not going to go back and re-read and try to understand.<br/><br/>This had an interesting premise. We have Jacob, who has been in foster care his entire life finally finding a home with Mr. Fielding. A car accident leaves Mr. Fielding dead ... and Jacob indestructible. Mr. Fielding told him so a split second before the accident. Apparently Mr. Fielding had been indes</span>
  <span id="freeText7697712132316795813" style="display:none">Huh ... I'm really not sure I understood what happened there in the last half of the book, but as I was pushing to even finish, I'm certainly not going to go back and re-read and try to understand.<br /><br />This had an interesting premise. We have Jacob, who has been in foster care his entire life finally finding a home with Mr. Fielding. A car accident leaves Mr. Fielding dead ... and Jacob indestructible. Mr. Fielding told him so a split second before the accident. Apparently Mr. Fielding had been indestructible, but transferred that power to Jacob to save his life. Jacob doesn't really realize anything (other than he shouldn't have survived) but when he accidentally transfers the power to someone else, and then witnesses an accident that should have caused extreme injury, he starts to put the pieces together. Jacob and his two friends (one he just met, but apparently falls for at first sight) then continue to experiment and try to use the power for good.<br /><br />I think I was okay with everything until about this point ... but then apparently, you aren't supposed to do that. People are supposed to die, and if you save them, it screws things up. There were strange metaphors about a "black lion" and as they uncover a confusing (to me) history and rules ...<br /><br />I don't know ... if you aren't supposed to use your "superpower" to help people, what is the point of it all? And then they have to "kill the darkness" out of Oh (and I wasn't found of that "name" either). Then there were weird relationships with the adults, only slightly in the picture (the priests, Mr. Coffin). I just had this confused and unhappy scrunched up face as I attempted to get through the last half of the book.<br /><br />... and the title (and changing countdown), what did that have to do with ANYTHING? </span>
  <a data-text-id="7697712132316795813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_159188520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159188520" />
    <a title="Ryan Zani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5055185-ryan-zani"><img alt="Ryan Zani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1299259458p2/5055185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159188520?book_show_action=true">Apr 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Zani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Zani" href="/user/show/5055185-ryan-zani">Ryan Zani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5055185-ryan-zani?shelf=independent-study">independent-study</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159188520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3379602816598009497">Plot: Jacobs father who adopted him at age 12 just died in a car crash with Jacob driving right before the crash Jacobs father tells Jacob these words "You are indestructible". Jacobs best friend Milo introduces him to a girl her name is Ophelia. They call her Oh and it is love at first sight Oh asks Jacob to sign her cast and Jacob signs "you are indestructible" and Oh gets into a long boarding accident that should have killed her but she got up without a scratch on her and they set off to find</span>
  <span id="freeText3379602816598009497" style="display:none">Plot: Jacobs father who adopted him at age 12 just died in a car crash with Jacob driving right before the crash Jacobs father tells Jacob these words "You are indestructible". Jacobs best friend Milo introduces him to a girl her name is Ophelia. They call her Oh and it is love at first sight Oh asks Jacob to sign her cast and Jacob signs "you are indestructible" and Oh gets into a long boarding accident that should have killed her but she got up without a scratch on her and they set off to find answers to their questions about the words "you are indestructible" <br />Elements and Style: Patrick Carman brings his favorite style of writing, mystery and brings it up a notch by adding a little bit of horror making it almost like a Halloween story. The rising action in this book seems to be very near the end of the book because it counts down from thirteen days to twelve days and so on and so forth and the setting is in my opinion the best setting in the world, Salem, Oregon they go to the Enchanted Forest even. The dialogue in this often switches from them taking to them recapping and often them texting.<br />Characterization: Jacob ( the main character ) is very relaxed but when stuff starts happening to his friends he gets pretty angry. He is was an orphan so its hard for him to talk about his (foster) dad especially when he is...well dead. He is very drastic in his emotions in the beginning he is very depressed because his dad is well, dead but in when he meets Ophelia (Oh) he becomes very happy but at the end of the story he is kind of in between because well... i don't want to ruin the story for you. <br /><br /> </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/546289825?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexis Villalobos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexis Villalobos" href="/user/show/13745680-alexis-villalobos">Alexis Villalobos</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer546289825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8848135883949489929">Thirteen Days to Midnight is a book filled with action, suspense, love, supernatural powers,etc. I really love how he starts off with an simple question:"If you could have one super power, what would it be?" After that little question, he runs with it. The book starts with Jacob who is returning to Holy Cross. His friend,Milo,is trying to get Jacob in the swing of things.once Milo tells Jacob about the new girl in town, he is hooked. He meets Ophelia James, a daring and beautiful girl. It first </span>
  <span id="freeText8848135883949489929" style="display:none">Thirteen Days to Midnight is a book filled with action, suspense, love, supernatural powers,etc. I really love how he starts off with an simple question:"If you could have one super power, what would it be?" After that little question, he runs with it. The book starts with Jacob who is returning to Holy Cross. His friend,Milo,is trying to get Jacob in the swing of things.once Milo tells Jacob about the new girl in town, he is hooked. He meets Ophelia James, a daring and beautiful girl. It first Jacob think she is a fragile girl. she had a pink cast on her arm. Jacob wrote the words on her cast he thought was necessary,"YOU ARE INDESTRUCTIBLE". When Ophelia wants shows she is daring girl, she does cement surfing. She takes a really bad fall. Expecting to see her with a broken, bloody body, she comes out with out a cut. While everyone is wondering how she is okay, Jacob thinks thins he knows why. After they get to know each other a little bit more, Jacob reveals his secret that he has kept with his since Mr. Fielding died. Saying the words,"YOU ARE INDESTRUCTIBLE", Jacob can save some one from dying. He had saved Ophelia from killing herself on the skate board. One they all take it in, they test it to see how it works. They use the Power to save themselves from trouble. Then Ophelia suggest the use the power to save people from facing death. This idea leads to some big problems. Jacob has to decide who lives and who dies. This is a amazing story that I would have not really picked up and read.I really recommend this book to people who like action, and supernatural powers. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8848135883949489929" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GVEj3HoempAdtP7SFXlTX4nbz4Y68BHgWCzFb0ik+Sgraxb2AKhACqU0KpPknBZiigRHbzOjGapmfQgi1+HItA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/46474.Patrick_Carman">About Patrick Carman</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10416308965222877602">I have been a lifelong writer and storyteller. Salem, Oregon is where I spent my formative years and I graduated from Willamette University. After college, I spent a decade living in Portland, Oregon where I worked in advertising, game design, and technology.<br/><br/>I've written young adult and children's books for Scholastic, Little Brown Books For Young Readers and Katherine Tegen Books/ HarperCollins P</span>
  <span id="freeText10416308965222877602" style="display:none">I have been a lifelong writer and storyteller. Salem, Oregon is where I spent my formative years and I graduated from Willamette University. After college, I spent a decade living in Portland, Oregon where I worked in advertising, game design, and technology.<br /><br />I've written young adult and children's books for Scholastic, Little Brown Books For Young Readers and Katherine Tegen Books/ HarperCollins Publishers.<br /><br />I've been fortunate enough to have had some bestselling series work: The Land of Elyon, Atherton, Elliot’s Park, 39 Clues, and Skeleton Creek. Here's a fun note...the books have been translated into approximately two dozen languages. Currently I'm developing a few new-media projects. Check out <a href="http://enterdarkeden.com" rel="nofollow noopener">DARK EDEN</a> to experience this type of cross-platform project.<br /><br />When I'm not writing or creating a story, I spend my free time supporting literacy campaigns and community organizations, fly fishing, playing basketball and tennis, doing crosswords, watching movies, dabbling in video games, reading (lots), and (more than anything else) spending time with my wife and two daughters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10416308965222877602" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
